        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42575678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8888611149238078539">The White Lioness, by Henning Mankell B-minus.<br/>Narrated by Dick Hill, produced by Blackstone audio, downloaded from audible.com<br/><br/>This is the first Mankell book that I’ve been disappointed with. In this book, Wallander and the national police force of Sweden inadvertently become involved in an assassination plot in South Africa. The perpetrators are being trained in Sweden. Wallander’s involvement begins when a man comes into his office and says that his wife, a real estate agent, has disappeared. S</span>
  <span id="freeText8888611149238078539" style="display:none">The White Lioness, by Henning Mankell B-minus.<br />Narrated by Dick Hill, produced by Blackstone audio, downloaded from audible.com<br /><br />This is the first Mankell book that I’ve been disappointed with. In this book, Wallander and the national police force of Sweden inadvertently become involved in an assassination plot in South Africa. The perpetrators are being trained in Sweden. Wallander’s involvement begins when a man comes into his office and says that his wife, a real estate agent, has disappeared. She was going to look at a house before showing it, and she never came back. After several days, her body was found, with one shot directly in the forehead, execution style. They soon come to believe she was only killed because she was at the wrong place at the wrong time, but what was really going on?<br /><br />This book was disappointing to me because it was not well organized. The parts involving South Africa were more like education material for the reader. But what was really off was Wallander. It’s clear he was losing it after he was responsible for killing a man. He was extremely depressed and was not acting rationally either in his personal life or in his investigations. What really didn’t work for me here was Wallander’s mood swings, and still being held up as a leader to the rest of the force. The chief, (I can’t remember what he’s really called) has always been shown as somewhat of a buffoon, but Wallander always goes his own way and doesn’t listen to orders given by the chief. In this book he does the same, but his own orders seem even more irrational than usual. I guess it doesn’t seem credible in this book that he would hold the respect he seems to hold by the police and even his enemies. <br />I think it is disappointing that Blackstone has chosen to have Dick Hill narrate the Mankell books. He overacts these books and triesto use what he thinks of as a Scandinavian accented English. It doesnt work.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8888611149238078539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_51268357" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51268357" />
    <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes"><img alt="Nancy Oakes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507555979p2/900340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51268357?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy Oakes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy Oakes" href="/user/show/900340-nancy-oakes">Nancy Oakes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781400031559" href="/book/show/922981.The_White_Lioness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=crime-fiction-scandinavia">crime-fiction-scandinavia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=translated-crime-fiction">translated-crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/900340-nancy-oakes?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51268357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8731709726934989823">The White Lioness is book number three in Mankell's series of crime novels Ystad detective featuring Kurt Wallander. I was really iffy on whether or not I would read this one, since it seemed more like a span-the-globe type of mystery, but I stuck with it and was happily rewarded. <br/><br/>The action begins when an estate agent goes out to look at a house for sale and loses her way on the road. Stopping to ask for directions at a farmhouse was the last thing she ever did. Called in to investigate her dis</span>
  <span id="freeText8731709726934989823" style="display:none">The White Lioness is book number three in Mankell's series of crime novels Ystad detective featuring Kurt Wallander. I was really iffy on whether or not I would read this one, since it seemed more like a span-the-globe type of mystery, but I stuck with it and was happily rewarded. <br /><br />The action begins when an estate agent goes out to look at a house for sale and loses her way on the road. Stopping to ask for directions at a farmhouse was the last thing she ever did. Called in to investigate her disappearance (and ultimately her death), Wallander and his team had no idea that their search for a killer would take them across the world to South Africa (the year is 1992), where a small cabal was planning a major assassination which its members hoped would set events in motion to stop the plans for disassembling the policy of apartheid in that country. This is one of those novels where you know who the killer is pretty much right away, and you're just watching to see how Wallander and his team figure it out. <br /><br />Well written, The White Lioness takes place in two separate settings, but the story is very neatly tied together. The characters are realistically drawn -- especially the character of Konovalenko, who makes for an excellent bad guy. I liked this one much better than the previous series entry (Dogs of Riga). I'd definitely recommend this one to fans of Mankell, to those who like Scandinavian mysteries (which, in my mind, are simply excellent), and to those readers who want a mystery novel that is engrossing. Fans of police procedurals will enjoy this book and this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8731709726934989823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2512141990" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2512141990" />

<div id="review_45578998" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45578998" />
    <a title="Bibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/422087-bibliophile"><img alt="Bibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238517395p2/422087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45578998?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibliophile" href="/user/show/422087-bibliophile">Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781400031559" href="/book/show/922981.The_White_Lioness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/422087-bibliophile?shelf=scandinavia">scandinavia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/422087-bibliophile?shelf=mystery-and-suspense">mystery-and-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/422087-bibliophile?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/422087-bibliophile?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45578998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8206340801132040327"><i>The White Lioness</i> is the third in Henning Mankell’s series of <i>romans policiers</i> starring the world-weary and digestively troubled Kurt Wallander. It’s 1993 and Nelson Mandela and F.W. de Klerk are negotiating the end to apartheid in South Africa. Meanwhile, in Ystad, Kurt Wallander is investigating the execution-style murder of a young housewife who seemingly had no flaws and no enemies. The two stories converge in an international intrigue a la <i>Day of the Jackal</i>. <br/><br/>I had several problems with this</span>
  <span id="freeText8206340801132040327" style="display:none"><i>The White Lioness</i> is the third in Henning Mankell’s series of <i>romans policiers</i> starring the world-weary and digestively troubled Kurt Wallander. It’s 1993 and Nelson Mandela and F.W. de Klerk are negotiating the end to apartheid in South Africa. Meanwhile, in Ystad, Kurt Wallander is investigating the execution-style murder of a young housewife who seemingly had no flaws and no enemies. The two stories converge in an international intrigue a la <i>Day of the Jackal</i>. <br /><br />I had several problems with this novel: first of all, Mankell’s writing style remains as flat and boring as ever – lots of declarative sentences, and spelling out what the characters are feeling in excruciating detail instead of letting the reader infer what he or she will from how they act/speak, etc. Apparently, “don’t show when you can spend pages telling” is Mankell’s style (or else he has a truly bad translator.) Secondly, this is the second book in a row in which Wallander is involved in massive international intrigue and I just don’t find this particularly believable. (The first novel of the series had an “ordinary” murder, but four of the five I’ve read – out of order – involve either James Bond-ish stuff or serial killers. This doesn’t strike me as realistic at all!) And lastly, and perhaps this is just because of when the novel was published and the assumption that lots of people didn't know what was going on in South Africa at the time, but the sections that don’t focus on Wallander are incredibly didactic – apartheid was a horrible regime that twisted people’s natural instincts and talents, some of the Afrikaners in South Africa were particularly manipulative and eeeevil, blahblah, I GET IT. I don’t need several hundred pages to tell me this!<br /><br />Now, I am a completist, so I’ll keep reading the remaining handful of novels in the series, but I’m definitely not impressed!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8206340801132040327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_716991122" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716991122" />
    <a title="Cathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/644703-cathy"><img alt="Cathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388698594p2/644703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716991122?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy" href="/user/show/644703-cathy">Cathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780786165377" href="/book/show/1438223.The_White_Lioness">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cathy by: </span>
      Professor Sid Bolkosky ז"ל had Henning Mankell books on his reading pile for a long time, and I took an interest.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/644703-cathy?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/644703-cathy?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716991122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5260707316767774954">Henning Mankell’s third Inspector Wallander mystery, The While Lioness, is a terrific blend of international thriller, human isolation and angst, and politics. Set at the end of South Africa’s Apartheid regime, after President de Klerk has called for an end to the racial laws governing the country and for free elections to follow, a group of Boers, Afrikaans, formed a secret committee to assassinate Nelson Mandela and create chaos in South Africa, thus allowing apartheid to continue. <br/><br/>A black Sou</span>
  <span id="freeText5260707316767774954" style="display:none">Henning Mankell’s third Inspector Wallander mystery, The While Lioness, is a terrific blend of international thriller, human isolation and angst, and politics. Set at the end of South Africa’s Apartheid regime, after President de Klerk has called for an end to the racial laws governing the country and for free elections to follow, a group of Boers, Afrikaans, formed a secret committee to assassinate Nelson Mandela and create chaos in South Africa, thus allowing apartheid to continue. <br /><br />A black South African hit man in sent to Sweden to train with a former KGB officer in a remote house near Ystad where Kurt Wallander is chief inspector. Wallander, who says of himself, "I'll never be any different than what I am. A pretty good cop in a medium-sized Swedish police district," is busy trying to solve the case of a real estate agent and mother, Louise Åkerblom, who was brutally murdered execution style and has no leads. In time Wallander comes to realize that the case of Louise Åkerblom is linked to the international conspiracy, but finding the perpetrators is impossible. Wallander becomes increasingly morose as he detaches himself from his police force and goes about finding the murderer on his own.<br /><br />What adds to the anticipation, even though we know the conclusion from a historical perspective, are the many mistakes that are made by members of the police force, staff in passport control, Interpol, and elsewhere. The book keeps you intrigued to the last minute. The narrator, Dick Hill, did a great job. While I was bothered by his voice on the first Wallander book because it reminded me of Lee Child’s character, Jack Reacher, he did a great job with the South African pronunciation, and I've now begun to associate him with Inspector Wallander. I'm now a committed fan of Henning Mankell. What took me so long?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5260707316767774954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9659601690489483648">This was a CD gift to me. I had not read Henning Mankell books before and now I will read his other novels. A murder happens quickly in the story and the hunt for the killer by Detective Kurt Wallander becomes intense and actually obsessive by the policeman. The problem I had was the introduction of so many characters from another location with another plot. The turns, twist, intertwining and ultimately the knitting together of each character is a feat accomplished by the author. The plot is abo</span>
  <span id="freeText9659601690489483648" style="display:none">This was a CD gift to me. I had not read Henning Mankell books before and now I will read his other novels. A murder happens quickly in the story and the hunt for the killer by Detective Kurt Wallander becomes intense and actually obsessive by the policeman. The problem I had was the introduction of so many characters from another location with another plot. The turns, twist, intertwining and ultimately the knitting together of each character is a feat accomplished by the author. The plot is about another murder plan in motion, one that will affect an entire nation and bring chaos to its citizens. Even after the story was done I find myself thinking of some of the characters. I'm hooked. The murder in the beginning is solved in the process. Confused as I became with the many characters and other plots, were satisfied and understood and therefore I will read and/or listen to another Mankell detective novel and I think for those who enjoy a "who done it" will want to engage themselves in this story. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3642395.The_Skye_in_June" title="The Skye in June by June Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">The Skye in June</a></span>

<div id="review_2575177075" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2575177075" />
    <a title="Gary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37678060-gary"><img alt="Gary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426717728p2/37678060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2575177075?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary" href="/user/show/37678060-gary">Gary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2575177075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6786738720832409443">An enjoyable read. Writing about real historical figures is dangerous but Mankell does it well. Having a plot rest on incomprehensibly stupid mistakes made by various characters is dangerous, and that can’t be done well. But maybe what I thought were stupid mistakes weren’t stupid or mistakes; maybe the incidents fit in the mindset of Sweden, not such a rough place as the world of American crime stories. Wondering about this adds a humane element I am glad I came to suspect. The characters, espe</span>
  <span id="freeText6786738720832409443" style="display:none">An enjoyable read. Writing about real historical figures is dangerous but Mankell does it well. Having a plot rest on incomprehensibly stupid mistakes made by various characters is dangerous, and that can’t be done well. But maybe what I thought were stupid mistakes weren’t stupid or mistakes; maybe the incidents fit in the mindset of Sweden, not such a rough place as the world of American crime stories. Wondering about this adds a humane element I am glad I came to suspect. The characters, especially Wallander, are the kind you absorb into yourself, though. Most of the plot was thoughtful, tight, adventurous. The moralizing is a little heavy, sometimes. The phrasing and the organization of the words, especially in the dialogue, have a likable, interesting quality and voice new to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6786738720832409443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('32nnHCvEs8Os2+EGhtC6xjuwjRQ4ZT5UflxDU84Pj69J456d8D8MsLPB7EZsAsiNG/8NrEfhl9uiuAscJZrPkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

On a July afternoon, a young woman\'s body is dred<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9182985426923704693\" style=\"display:none\">The masterful first novel in the Martin Beck series of mysteries by the internationally renowned crime writing duo Maj Sjöwall and Per Wahlöö, finds Beck hunting for the murderer of a lonely traveler. On a July afternoon, a young woman\'s body is dredged from Sweden\'s beautiful Lake Vattern. With no clues Beck begins an investigation not only to uncover a murderer but also to discover who the victim was. Three months later, all Beck knows is that her name was Roseanna and that she could have been strangled by any one of eighty-five people on a cruise. As the melancholic Beck narrows the list of suspects, he is drawn increasingly to the enigma of the victim, a free-spirited traveler with a penchant for casual sex, and to the psychopathology of a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11242840507041397854">Henning Mankell was an internationally known Swedish crime writer, children's author and playwright. He was best known for his literary character Kurt Wallander.<br/><br/>Mankell split his time between Sweden and Mozambique. He was married to Eva Bergman, Swedish director and daughter of Ingmar Bergman.</span>

But his investigation is beset with a handful of obstacles—a department distracted by the threat of impending cutbacks and the frivolity of World Cup soccer, a tenuous long-distance relationship with a murdered policeman’s widow, and the unshakably haunting preoccupation with the young girl who set herself on fire. And so, with his inimitable disregard for normal procedure, Wallander is soon interfering in matters that are not his responsibility, making promises he won’t keep, telling lies when it suits him—and getting results. But the results hint at elaborate Cold War espionage activities that seem inextricably confounding, even to Wallander, who, in any case, is troubled in more personal ways as well. Negligent of his health, he’s become convinced that, having turned sixty, he is on the threshold of senility.
